# Searching Sourcegraph

Search before you build. Existing patterns reduce tokens, ensure consistency, and surface tested solutions.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Tool Selection Logic

**Start here:**

1. **Know the exact symbol or pattern?** → `sg_keyword_search`
2. **Know the concept, not the code?** → `sg_nls_search`
3. **Need to understand how/why?** → `sg_deepsearch_read`
4. **Tracing a symbol's usage?** → `sg_find_references`
5. **Need full implementation?** → `sg_go_to_definition` → `sg_read_file`

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Exact code patterns | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Trace usage | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Understand systems | `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Read files | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
file:.*\.test\.ts$ -file:__mocks__   # Tests, exclude mocks
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

Combine filters: `repo:^github.com/myorg/backend$ file:src/handlers lang:typescript`

## Context-Aware Behaviour

**When the user provides a file path or error message:**
- Extract symbols, function names, or error codes
- Search for those exact terms first
- Trace references if the error involves a known symbol

**When the user asks "how does X work":**
- Prefer `sg_deepsearch_read` for architectural understanding
- Follow up with `sg_read_file` on key files mentioned in the response

**When the user is implementing a new feature:**
- Search for similar existing implementations first
- Read tests for usage examples
- Check for shared utilities before creating new ones

**When debugging:**
- Search for the exact error string
- Trace the symbol where the error is thrown
- Check recent changes with `sg_diff_search`

## Workflows

For detailed step-by-step workflows, see:
- `workflows/implementing-feature.md` — when building new features
- `workflows/understanding-code.md` — when exploring unfamiliar systems
- `workflows/debugging-issue.md` — when tracking down bugs

## Efficiency Rules

**Minimise tool calls:**
- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms (faster, more precise)

**Batch your understanding:**
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than reading one and asking questions
- Use `sg_deepsearch_read` for "how does X work" instead of multiple keyword searches

**Avoid common token waste:**
- Don't search all repos when you know the target repo
- Don't use `sg_deepsearch_read` for simple "find all" queries
- Don't re-read files you've already seen in this conversation

## Query Patterns

| Intent | Query |
|--------|-------|
| React hooks | `file:.*\.tsx$ use[A-Z].*= \(` |
| API routes | `file:src/api app\.(get\|post\|put\|delete)` |
| Error handling | `catch.*Error\|\.catch\(` |
| Type definitions | `file:types/ export (interface\|type)` |
| Test setup | `file:.*\.test\. beforeEach\|beforeAll` |
| Config files | `file:(webpack\|vite\|rollup)\.config` |
| CI/CD | `file:\.github/workflows deploy` |

For more patterns, see `query-patterns.md`.

## Output Formatting

**Search results:**
- Present as a brief summary, not raw tool output
- Highlight the most relevant file and line
- Include a code snippet only if it directly answers the question

**Code explanations:**
- Start with a one-sentence summary
- Use the codebase's own terminology
- Reference specific files and functions

**Recommendations:**
- Present as numbered steps if actionable
- Link to specific patterns found in the codebase
- Note any existing utilities that should be reused

## Common Mistakes

| Mistake | Fix |
|---------|-----|
| Searching all repos | Add `repo:^github.com/org/repo$` |
| Too many results | Add `file:` pattern or keywords |
| Missing relevant code | Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching |
| Not understanding context | Use `sg_deepsearch_read` |
| Guessing patterns | Read implementations with `sg_read_file` |

## Principles

- Start narrow, expand if needed
- Chain tools: search → read → find references → definition
- Check tests for usage examples
- Read before generating

# Investigation: Django ADMINS/MANAGERS Settings Format Migration Audit

**Repository:** django/django
**Task Type:** Migration Audit (investigation only — no code changes)

## Scenario

Django is changing the `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` settings from their current format of `[(name, email), ...]` tuples to simple `[email, ...]` string lists. This is tracked in ticket #36138. Before executing this migration, the team needs a comprehensive audit of all code that reads, validates, or processes these settings.

## Your Task

Produce a migration audit report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. Every file that reads `settings.ADMINS` or `settings.MANAGERS`
2. Every file that validates or type-checks the settings format
3. Every file that unpacks the tuple format (e.g., `for name, email in settings.ADMINS`)
4. All documentation references that show the old tuple format
5. Test files that use the old format in fixtures or assertions
6. Third-party compatibility concerns (what breaks for users with old-format settings)
7. A migration checklist: each file that needs changes, what change is needed

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Core code paths that consume the tuple format>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of modules/packages impacted>

## Recommendation
<Migration checklist with specific files and changes needed>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on `django/core/mail/`, test files, and documentation

72-assistanttext-
The investigation report has been written to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. Here is a summary of the findings:

## Investigation Summary

**Status:** The `ADMINS`/`MANAGERS` format migration is already partially complete as of Django 6.0. The tuple format `[(name, email), ...]` was deprecated with `RemovedInDjango70Warning` and will be fully removed in Django 7.0.

### Key Findings

**Central code path** (`django/core/mail/__init__.py:152-191`):
- All consumption of `ADMINS`/`MANAGERS` flows through `_send_server_message()`.
- This function contains the **only tuple-unpacking logic** at line 173: `recipients = [a[1] for a in recipients]`.
- The backward-compatibility shim (lines 165-173) is the sole location needing removal in Django 7.0.

**Other files** that access `settings.ADMINS`:
- `django/utils/log.py:97` — truthiness check only (`if not settings.ADMINS`), no unpacking.

**Documentation** — fully migrated: `docs/ref/settings.txt` shows the new string format with `versionchanged:: 6.0` notes.

**Tests** — `tests/mail/tests.py:2402` contains `test_deprecated_admins_managers_tuples` (marked for removal) and `test_wrong_admins_managers` has commented-out cases to uncomment when support ends.

### Migration Checklist for Django 7.0

1. **`django/core/mail/__init__.py`** — Remove lines 165-173 (the `RemovedInDjango70Warning` backward-compat block).
2. **`tests/mail/tests.py`** — Delete `test_deprecated_admins_managers_tuples` (line 2402); uncomment tuple cases in `test_wrong_admins_managers` (lines 2432-2441).
3. **`docs/ref/settings.txt`** — Optionally remove `versionchanged:: 6.0` notes from ADMINS/MANAGERS entries.
4. **`docs/releases/7.0.txt`** — Document the breaking change.

  "content": "# Investigation Report\n\n## Summary\n\nDjango 6.0 introduced a deprecation (tracked as `RemovedInDjango70Warning`) of the old `ADMINS`/`MANAGERS` format \u2014 lists of `(name, email)` tuples \u2014 in favor of plain email address strings. The migration is already partially complete: the new format is enforced in `django/core/mail/__init__.py` with backward-compatible fallback logic, documentation has been updated, and tests have been written for both old and new formats. The remaining work for Django 7.0 is to remove the backward-compatibility shim and finalize validation.\n\n---\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe core consumption of `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` is centralized in a single internal function, `_send_server_message()`, in `django/core/mail/__init__.py` (lines 152\u2013191). Both public functions `mail_admins()` and `mail_managers()` delegate to this helper. The function:\n\n1. Reads the setting via `getattr(settings, setting_name)`.\n2. **Detects the old tuple format** (lines 166\u2013173): if all items are 2-element lists or tuples, it emits a `RemovedInDjango70Warning` and extracts the email address as `a[1]`.\n3. **Validates the new format** (lines 175\u2013180): raises `ImproperlyConfigured` if the value is not a list/tuple of strings or `Promise` objects.\n4. Sends the email using `EmailMultiAlternatives`.\n\nThe `AdminEmailHandler.emit()` in `django/utils/log.py` (line 97) accesses `settings.ADMINS` directly for an early-return optimization (checking if the list is empty/falsy), but does not unpack the tuple format itself \u2014 it delegates to `mail.mail_admins()`.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Files That Read `settings.ADMINS` or # Investigation Report

## Summary

Django 6.0 introduced a deprecation (tracked as `RemovedInDjango70Warning`) of the old `ADMINS`/`MANAGERS` format — lists of `(name, email)` tuples — in favor of plain email address strings. The migration is already partially complete: the new format is enforced in `django/core/mail/__init__.py` with backward-compatible fallback logic, documentation has been updated, and tests have been written for both old and new formats. The remaining work for Django 7.0 is to remove the backward-compatibility shim and finalize validation.

---

## Root Cause

The core consumption of `ADMINS` and `MANAGERS` is centralized in a single internal function, `_send_server_message()`, in `django/core/mail/__init__.py` (lines 152–191). Both public functions `mail_admins()` and `mail_managers()` delegate to this helper. The function:

1. Reads the setting via `getattr(settings, setting_name)`.
2. **Detects the old tuple format** (lines 166–173): if all items are 2-element lists or tuples, it emits a `RemovedInDjango70Warning` and extracts the email address as `a[1]`.
3. **Validates the new format** (lines 175–180): raises `ImproperlyConfigured` if the value is not a list/tuple of strings or `Promise` objects.
4. Sends the email using `EmailMultiAlternatives`.

The `AdminEmailHandler.emit()` in `django/utils/log.py` (line 97) accesses `settings.ADMINS` directly for an early-return optimization (checking if the list is empty/falsy), but does not unpack the tuple format itself — it delegates to `mail.mail_admins()`.

---

## Evidence

### Files That Read `settings.ADMINS` or `settings.MANAGERS`

| File | Line(s) | How Used |
|------|---------|----------|
| `django/core/mail/__init__.py` | 161 | `getattr(settings, setting_name)` — reads both ADMINS and MANAGERS
... (truncated)
